Some tracks were composed using Eno and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Schmidt_(artist)" title="Peter Schmidt (artist)">Peter Schmidt</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Oblique_Strategies" title="Oblique Strategies">Oblique Strategies</a> cards: "Boys Keep Swinging" entailed band members swapping instruments, "Move On" used the chords from Bowie's early composition "All the Young Dudes" played backwards, and "Red Money" took backing tracks from "Sister Midnight", a piece previously composed with Iggy Pop.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The album was recorded in Switzerland. Ahead of its release, RCA's Mel Ilberman stated, "It would be fair to call it Bowie's <i><a href="/wiki/Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band" title="Sgt. Pepper&#39;s Lonely Hearts Club Band">Sergeant Pepper</a></i>&#160;... a concept album that portrays the Lodger as a homeless wanderer, shunned and victimized by life's pressures and technology." As described by biographer Christopher Sandford, "The record dashed such high hopes with dubious choices, and production that spelt the end—for fifteen years—of Bowie's partnership with Eno." <i>Lodger</i> reached No. 4 in the UK and No. 20 in the US, and yielded the UK hit singles "<a href="/wiki/Boys_Keep_Swinging" title="Boys Keep Swinging">Boys Keep Swinging</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/DJ_(David_Bowie_song)" title="DJ (David Bowie song)">DJ</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lodger_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lodger-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Towards the end of the year, Bowie and Angie initiated divorce proceedings, and after months of court battles the marriage was ended in early 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1980.E2.80.931988:_New_Romantic_and_pop_era"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1980–1988:_New_Romantic_and_pop_era">1980–1988: New Romantic and pop era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Bowie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1980–1988: New Romantic and pop era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bowie_1983_serious_moonlight.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Bowie_1983_serious_moonlight.jpg/170px-Bowie_1983_serious_moonlight.jpg" width="170" height="410" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Bowie_1983_serious_moonlight.jpg/255px-Bowie_1983_serious_moonlight.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Bowie_1983_serious_moonlight.jpg/340px-Bowie_1983_serious_moonlight.jpg 2x" data-file-width="610" data-file-height="1472" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bowie_1983_serious_moonlight.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Serious_Moonlight_Tour" title="Serious Moonlight Tour">Serious Moonlight Tour</a>, 1983</div></div></div>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Scary_Monsters_and_Super_Creeps" class="mw-redirect" title="Scary Monsters and Super Creeps">Scary Monsters and Super Creeps</a></i> (1980) produced the number-one hit "<a href="/wiki/Ashes_to_Ashes_(David_Bowie_song)" title="Ashes to Ashes (David Bowie song)">Ashes to Ashes</a>", featuring the textural work of guitar-synthesist <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Hammer" title="Chuck Hammer">Chuck Hammer</a> and revisiting the character of Major Tom from "Space Oddity". The song gave international exposure to the underground <a href="/wiki/New_Romantic" title="New Romantic">New Romantic</a> movement when Bowie visited the London club "Blitz"—the main New Romantic hangout—to recruit several of the regulars (including <a href="/wiki/Steve_Strange" title="Steve Strange">Steve Strange</a> of the band <a href="/wiki/Visage_(band)" title="Visage (band)">Visage</a>) to act in the accompanying video, renowned as one of the most innovative of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> While <i>Scary Monsters</i> used principles established by the Berlin albums, it was considered by critics to be far more direct musically and lyrically. The album's hard rock edge included conspicuous guitar contributions from <a href="/wiki/Robert_Fripp" title="Robert Fripp">Robert Fripp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Hammer" title="Chuck Hammer">Chuck Hammer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pete_Townshend" title="Pete Townshend">Pete Townshend</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> As "Ashes to Ashes" hit number one on the UK charts, Bowie opened a three-month run on Broadway on 24 September, starring as <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Merrick" title="Joseph Merrick">John Merrick</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Elephant_Man_(play)" title="The Elephant Man (play)">The Elephant Man</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-elephantman_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elephantman-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bowie paired with <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a> in 1981 for a one-off single release, "<a href="/wiki/Under_Pressure" title="Under Pressure">Under Pressure</a>". The duet was a hit, becoming Bowie's third UK number-one single. Bowie was given the lead role in the BBC's 1982 televised adaptation of <a href="/wiki/Bertolt_Brecht" title="Bertolt Brecht">Bertolt Brecht</a>'s play <i><a href="/wiki/Baal_(play)" title="Baal (play)">Baal</a></i>. Coinciding with its transmission, a five-track <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">EP</a> of songs from the play, recorded earlier in Berlin, was released as <i><a href="/wiki/Baal_(EP)" title="Baal (EP)">David Bowie in Bertolt Brecht's Baal</a></i>. In March 1982, the month before <a href="/wiki/Paul_Schrader" title="Paul Schrader">Paul Schrader</a>'s film <i><a href="/wiki/Cat_People_(1982_film)" title="Cat People (1982 film)">Cat People</a></i> came out, Bowie's title song, "<a href="/wiki/Cat_People_(Putting_Out_Fire)" title="Cat People (Putting Out Fire)">Cat People (Putting Out Fire)</a>", was released as a single, becoming a minor US hit and entering the UK Top 30.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bowie reached his peak of popularity and commercial success in 1983 with <i><a href="/wiki/Let%27s_Dance_(David_Bowie_album)" title="Let&#39;s Dance (David Bowie album)">Let's Dance</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Co-produced by <a href="/wiki/Chic_(band)" title="Chic (band)">Chic</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Nile_Rodgers" title="Nile Rodgers">Nile Rodgers</a>, the album went platinum in both the UK and the US. Its three singles became Top 20 hits in both countries, where its <a href="/wiki/Let%27s_Dance_(David_Bowie_song)" title="Let&#39;s Dance (David Bowie song)">title track</a> reached number one. "<a href="/wiki/Modern_Love_(song)" title="Modern Love (song)">Modern Love</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/China_Girl_(song)" title="China Girl (song)">China Girl</a>" each made No. 2 in the UK, accompanied by a pair of "absorbing" promotional videos that biographer David Buckley said "activated key archetypes in the pop world. 'Let's Dance', with its little narrative surrounding the young <a href="/wiki/Aboriginal_Australians" title="Aboriginal Australians">Aborigine</a> couple, targeted 'youth', and 'China Girl', with its bare-bummed (and later partially censored) beach lovemaking scene (a homage to the film <i><a href="/wiki/From_Here_to_Eternity" title="From Here to Eternity">From Here to Eternity</a></i>), was sufficiently sexually provocative to guarantee heavy rotation on MTV".<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Ray_Vaughan" title="Stevie Ray Vaughan">Stevie Ray Vaughan</a> was guest guitarist playing solo on "Let's Dance", although the video depicts Bowie miming this part.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> By 1983, Bowie had emerged as one of the most important video artists of the day. <i>Let's Dance</i> was followed by the <a href="/wiki/Serious_Moonlight_Tour" title="Serious Moonlight Tour">Serious Moonlight Tour</a>, during which Bowie was accompanied by guitarist <a href="/wiki/Earl_Slick" title="Earl Slick">Earl Slick</a> and backing vocalists <a href="/wiki/The_Simms_Brothers_Band" title="The Simms Brothers Band">Frank and George Simms</a>. The world tour lasted six months and was extremely popular."<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/1984_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="1984 MTV Video Music Awards">1984 MTV Video Music Awards</a> Bowie received two awards including the inaugural <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson_Video_Vanguard_Award" title="Michael Jackson Video Vanguard Award">Video Vanguard Award</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:David_Bowie_(1987).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/David_Bowie_%281987%29.jpg/170px-David_Bowie_%281987%29.jpg" width="170" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/David_Bowie_%281987%29.jpg/255px-David_Bowie_%281987%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/David_Bowie_%281987%29.jpg/340px-David_Bowie_%281987%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="761" data-file-height="945" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:David_Bowie_(1987).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bowie performing during the <a href="/wiki/Glass_Spider_Tour" title="Glass Spider Tour">Glass Spider Tour</a>, 1987</div></div></div>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Tonight_(David_Bowie_album)" title="Tonight (David Bowie album)">Tonight</a></i> (1984), another dance-oriented album, found Bowie collaborating with <a href="/wiki/Tina_Turner" title="Tina Turner">Tina Turner</a> and, once again, Iggy Pop. It included a number of cover songs, among them the 1966 <a href="/wiki/The_Beach_Boys" title="The Beach Boys">Beach Boys</a> hit "<a href="/wiki/God_Only_Knows" title="God Only Knows">God Only Knows</a>". The album bore the transatlantic Top 10 hit "<a href="/wiki/Blue_Jean_(song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Blue Jean (song)">Blue Jean</a>", itself the inspiration for a short film that won Bowie a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Music_Video" title="Grammy Award for Best Music Video">Grammy Award for Best Short Form Music Video</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Jazzin%27_for_Blue_Jean" title="Jazzin&#39; for Blue Jean">Jazzin' for Blue Jean</a></i>. Bowie performed at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley Stadium</a> in 1985 for <a href="/wiki/Live_Aid" title="Live Aid">Live Aid</a>, a multi-venue benefit concert for Ethiopian famine relief.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> During the event, the video for a fundraising single was premiered, Bowie's duet with <a href="/wiki/Mick_Jagger" title="Mick Jagger">Mick Jagger</a>. "<a href="/wiki/Dancing_in_the_Street" title="Dancing in the Street">Dancing in the Street</a>" quickly went to number one on release. The same year, Bowie worked with the <a href="/wiki/Pat_Metheny_Group" title="Pat Metheny Group">Pat Metheny Group</a> to record "<a href="/wiki/This_Is_Not_America" title="This Is Not America">This Is Not America</a>" for the soundtrack of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Falcon_and_the_Snowman" title="The Falcon and the Snowman">The Falcon and the Snowman</a></i>. Released as a single, the song became a Top 40 hit in the UK and US.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bowie was given a role in the 1986 film <i><a href="/wiki/Absolute_Beginners_(film)" title="Absolute Beginners (film)">Absolute Beginners</a></i>. It was poorly received by critics, but Bowie's <a href="/wiki/Theme_music" title="Theme music">theme song</a>, also named "<a href="/wiki/Absolute_Beginners_(David_Bowie_song)" title="Absolute Beginners (David Bowie song)">Absolute Beginners</a>", rose to No. 2 in the UK charts. He also appeared as <a href="/wiki/Jareth" title="Jareth">Jareth</a>, the Goblin King, in the 1986 <a href="/wiki/Jim_Henson" title="Jim Henson">Jim Henson</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Labyrinth_(film)" title="Labyrinth (film)">Labyrinth</a></i>, for which he wrote five songs. His final solo album of the decade was 1987's <i><a href="/wiki/Never_Let_Me_Down" title="Never Let Me Down">Never Let Me Down</a></i>, where he ditched the light sound of his previous two albums, instead offering harder rock with an <a href="/wiki/Industrial_music" title="Industrial music">industrial</a>/<a href="/wiki/Techno" title="Techno">techno</a> dance edge. Peaking at No. 6 in the UK, the album yielded the hits "<a href="/wiki/Day-In_Day-Out" title="Day-In Day-Out">Day-In, Day-Out</a>" (his 60th single), "<a href="/wiki/Time_Will_Crawl" title="Time Will Crawl">Time Will Crawl</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Never_Let_Me_Down_(David_Bowie_song)" title="Never Let Me Down (David Bowie song)">Never Let Me Down</a>". Bowie later described it as his "nadir", calling it "an awful album".<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Supporting <i>Never Let Me Down</i>, and preceded by nine promotional press shows, the 86-concert <a href="/wiki/Glass_Spider_Tour" title="Glass Spider Tour">Glass Spider Tour</a> commenced on 30 May. Bowie's backing band included <a href="/wiki/Peter_Frampton" title="Peter Frampton">Peter Frampton</a> on lead guitar. Contemporary critics maligned the tour as overproduced, saying it pandered to the current <a href="/wiki/Arena_rock" title="Arena rock">stadium rock</a> trends in its special effects and dancing,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> although years after the tour's conclusion, critics acknowledged that the tour influenced how other artists performed concerts, including <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a>, and <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC09_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC09-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1989.E2.80.931991:_Tin_Machine"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1989–1991:_Tin_Machine">1989–1991: Tin Machine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Bowie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 1989–1991: Tin Machine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tin_Machine" title="Tin Machine">Tin Machine</a></div>
<p>Bowie shelved his solo career in 1989, retreating to the relative anonymity of band membership for the first time since the early 1970s. A hard-rocking quartet, <a href="/wiki/Tin_Machine" title="Tin Machine">Tin Machine</a> came into being after Bowie began to work experimentally with guitarist <a href="/wiki/Reeves_Gabrels" title="Reeves Gabrels">Reeves Gabrels</a>. The line-up was completed by <a href="/wiki/Tony_Fox_Sales" title="Tony Fox Sales">Tony</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hunt_Sales" title="Hunt Sales">Hunt Sales</a>, whom Bowie had known since the late 1970s for their contribution, on bass and drums respectively, to Iggy Pop's 1977 album <i>Lust for Life</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:David_Bowie_Chile.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/David_Bowie_Chile.jpg/170px-David_Bowie_Chile.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/David_Bowie_Chile.jpg/255px-David_Bowie_Chile.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/David_Bowie_Chile.jpg/340px-David_Bowie_Chile.jpg 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:David_Bowie_Chile.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bowie in Chile during the <a href="/wiki/Sound%2BVision_Tour" title="Sound+Vision Tour">Sound+Vision Tour</a>, 1990</div></div></div>
<p>Although he intended Tin Machine to operate as a democracy, Bowie dominated, both in songwriting and in decision-making.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> The band's album debut, <i><a href="/wiki/Tin_Machine_(album)" title="Tin Machine (album)">Tin Machine</a></i> (1989), was initially popular, though its politicised lyrics did not find universal approval: Bowie described one song as "a simplistic, naive, radical, laying-it-down about the emergence of <a href="/wiki/Neo-Nazism" title="Neo-Nazism">Neo-Nazis</a>"; in the view of biographer Christopher Sandford, "It took nerve to denounce drugs, fascism and TV&#160;... in terms that reached the literary level of a comic book."<sup id="cite_ref-tinmachine1_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tinmachine1-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> EMI complained of "lyrics that preach" as well as "repetitive tunes" and "minimalist or no production".<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> The album nevertheless reached No. 3 and went gold in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-tinmachine1_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tinmachine1-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Tin Machine's first world tour was a commercial success, but there was growing reluctance—among fans and critics alike—to accept Bowie's presentation as merely a band member.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> A series of Tin Machine singles failed to chart, and Bowie, after a disagreement with EMI, left the label.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> Like his audience and his critics, Bowie himself became increasingly disaffected with his role as just one member of a band.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Tin Machine began work on a second album, but Bowie put the venture on hold and made a return to solo work. Performing his early hits during the seven-month <a href="/wiki/Sound%2BVision_Tour" title="Sound+Vision Tour">Sound+Vision Tour</a>, he found commercial success and acclaim once again.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 1990, a decade after his divorce from Angie, Bowie and <a href="/wiki/Somalis" title="Somalis">Somali</a>-born supermodel <a href="/wiki/Iman_(model)" title="Iman (model)">Iman</a> were introduced by a mutual friend. Bowie recalled, "I was naming the children the night we met&#160;... it was absolutely immediate." They married in 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Tin Machine resumed work the same month, but their audience and critics, ultimately left disappointed by the first album, showed little interest in a second. <i><a href="/wiki/Tin_Machine_II" title="Tin Machine II">Tin Machine II</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s arrival was marked by a widely publicised and ill-timed conflict over the cover art: after production had begun, the new record label, <a href="/wiki/Victory_Records" title="Victory Records">Victory</a>, deemed the depiction of four ancient nude <a href="/wiki/Kouros" title="Kouros">Kouroi</a> statues, judged by Bowie to be "in exquisite taste", "a show of wrong, obscene images", requiring air-brushing and patching to render the figures sexless.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> Tin Machine toured again, but after the live album <i><a href="/wiki/Tin_Machine_Live:_Oy_Vey,_Baby" title="Tin Machine Live: Oy Vey, Baby">Tin Machine Live: Oy Vey, Baby</a></i> failed commercially, the band drifted apart, and Bowie, though he continued to collaborate with Gabrels, resumed his solo career.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1992.E2.80.931998:_Electronic_period"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1992–1998:_Electronic_period">1992–1998: Electronic period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Bowie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 1992–1998: Electronic period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 20 April 1992, Bowie appeared at <a href="/wiki/The_Freddie_Mercury_Tribute_Concert" title="The Freddie Mercury Tribute Concert">The Freddie Mercury Tribute Concert</a>, following the Queen singer's death the previous year. As well as performing "Heroes" and "All the Young Dudes", he was joined on "Under Pressure" by <a href="/wiki/Annie_Lennox" title="Annie Lennox">Annie Lennox</a>, who took Mercury's vocal part; during his appearance, Bowie knelt and recited the <a href="/wiki/Lord%27s_Prayer" title="Lord&#39;s Prayer">Lord's Prayer</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LA_Times_Mercury_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LA_Times_Mercury-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Four days later, Bowie and Iman were married in Switzerland. Intending to move to Los Angeles, they flew in to search for a suitable property, but found themselves confined to their hotel, under curfew: the <a href="/wiki/1992_Los_Angeles_riots" title="1992 Los Angeles riots">1992 Los Angeles riots</a> began the day they arrived. They settled in New York instead.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:David_Bowie_1997.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/David_Bowie_1997.jpg/170px-David_Bowie_1997.jpg" width="170" height="259" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/David_Bowie_1997.jpg/255px-David_Bowie_1997.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/David_Bowie_1997.jpg/340px-David_Bowie_1997.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1292" data-file-height="1967" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:David_Bowie_1997.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bowie performing in <a href="/wiki/Turku" title="Turku">Turku</a>, Finland, 1997</div></div></div>
<p>In 1993, Bowie released his first solo offering since his Tin Machine departure, the soul, jazz, and <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip-hop</a> influenced <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Tie_White_Noise" title="Black Tie White Noise">Black Tie White Noise</a></i>. Making prominent use of electronic instruments, the album, which reunited Bowie with <i>Let's Dance</i> producer <a href="/wiki/Nile_Rodgers" title="Nile Rodgers">Nile Rodgers</a>, confirmed Bowie's return to popularity, hitting the number-one spot on the UK charts and spawning three Top 40 hits, including the Top 10 single "<a href="/wiki/Jump_They_Say" title="Jump They Say">Jump They Say</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Bowie explored new directions on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Buddha_of_Suburbia_(soundtrack)" title="The Buddha of Suburbia (soundtrack)">The Buddha of Suburbia</a></i> (1993), ostensibly a soundtrack album of his music composed for the BBC television adaptation of <a href="/wiki/The_Buddha_of_Suburbia_(novel)" title="The Buddha of Suburbia (novel)">Hanif Kureishi's novel</a>. Only the title track had been used in the television adaptation, although some of his <a href="/wiki/Subject_(music)" title="Subject (music)">themes</a> for it were also present on the album.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> It contained some of the new elements introduced in <i>Black Tie White Noise</i>, and also signalled a move towards <a href="/wiki/Alternative_rock" title="Alternative rock">alternative rock</a>. The album was a critical success but received a low-key release and only made No. 87 in the UK charts.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Reuniting Bowie with Eno, the quasi-<a href="/wiki/Industrial_music" title="Industrial music">industrial</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Outside_(David_Bowie_album)" title="Outside (David Bowie album)">Outside</a></i> (1995) was originally conceived as the first volume in a non-linear narrative of art and murder. Featuring characters from a short story written by Bowie, the album achieved UK and US chart success, and yielded three Top 40 UK singles.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> In a move that provoked mixed reaction from both fans and critics, Bowie chose <a href="/wiki/Nine_Inch_Nails" title="Nine Inch Nails">Nine Inch Nails</a> as his tour partner for the <a href="/wiki/Outside_Tour" title="Outside Tour">Outside Tour</a>. Visiting cities in Europe and North America between September 1995 and February 1996, the tour saw the return of Gabrels as Bowie's guitarist.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> On 7 January 1997, Bowie celebrated his half century with a 50th birthday concert at <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a>, New York, at which he was joined in playing his songs and those of his guests, Lou Reed, <a href="/wiki/Dave_Grohl" title="Dave Grohl">Dave Grohl</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Foo_Fighters" title="Foo Fighters">Foo Fighters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Smith_(musician)" title="Robert Smith (musician)">Robert Smith</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Cure" title="The Cure">the Cure</a>, <a href="/wiki/Billy_Corgan" title="Billy Corgan">Billy Corgan</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Smashing_Pumpkins" title="The Smashing Pumpkins">the Smashing Pumpkins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_Francis" title="Black Francis">Black Francis</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Pixies" title="Pixies">Pixies</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sonic_Youth" title="Sonic Youth">Sonic Youth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bowie was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> on 17 January 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-rockhall_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rockhall-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Incorporating experiments in British jungle and <a href="/wiki/Drum_and_bass" title="Drum and bass">drum 'n' bass</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Earthling_(album)" title="Earthling (album)">Earthling</a></i> (1997) was a critical and commercial success in the UK and the US, and two singles from the album – "<a href="/wiki/Little_Wonder_(song)" title="Little Wonder (song)">Little Wonder</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Dead_Man_Walking_(song)" title="Dead Man Walking (song)">Dead Man Walking</a>" – became UK Top 40 hits. Bowie's song "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_Afraid_of_Americans" title="I&#39;m Afraid of Americans">I'm Afraid of Americans</a>" from the <a href="/wiki/Paul_Verhoeven" title="Paul Verhoeven">Paul Verhoeven</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Showgirls" title="Showgirls">Showgirls</a></i> was re-recorded for the album, and remixed by <a href="/wiki/Trent_Reznor" title="Trent Reznor">Trent Reznor</a> for a single release. The heavy rotation of the accompanying video, also featuring <a href="/wiki/Trent_Reznor" title="Trent Reznor">Trent Reznor</a>, contributed to the song's 16-week stay in the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>. Bowie received a star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a> on 12 February 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-DB97x_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DB97x-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Earthling_Tour" title="Earthling Tour">Earthling Tour</a> took in Europe and North America between June and November 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-Buckley_pp._533–34_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Buckley_pp._533–34-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> In November 1997, Bowie performed on the BBC's <a href="/wiki/Children_in_Need" title="Children in Need">Children in Need</a> charity single "<a href="/wiki/Perfect_Day_97" class="mw-redirect" title="Perfect Day 97">Perfect Day</a>", which reached number one in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> Bowie reunited with Visconti in 1998 to record "(Safe in This) Sky Life" for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rugrats_Movie" title="The Rugrats Movie">The Rugrats Movie</a></i>. Although the track was edited out of the final cut, it was later re-recorded and released as "Safe" on the B-side of Bowie's 2002 single "<a href="/wiki/Everyone_Says_%27Hi%27" title="Everyone Says &#39;Hi&#39;">Everyone Says 'Hi'</a><span style="padding-left:.2em;">"</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> The reunion led to other collaborations including a limited-edition single release version of <a href="/wiki/Placebo_(band)" title="Placebo (band)">Placebo's</a> track "<a href="/wiki/Without_You_I%27m_Nothing_(song)" title="Without You I&#39;m Nothing (song)">Without You I'm Nothing</a>", co-produced by Visconti, with Bowie's harmonised vocal added to the original recording.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bowie_Bonds">Bowie Bonds</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Bowie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Bowie Bonds">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Bowie Bonds, an early example of <a href="/wiki/Celebrity_bond" title="Celebrity bond">celebrity bonds</a>, were <a href="/wiki/Asset-backed_security" title="Asset-backed security">asset-backed securities</a> of current and future revenues of the 25 albums (287 songs) that Bowie recorded before 1990. Bowie Bonds were pioneered by <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock and roll</a> <a href="/wiki/Investment_banking" title="Investment banking">investment banker</a> David Pullman.<sup id="cite_ref-Investment_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Investment-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Issued in 1997, the bonds were bought for US$55 million by the <a href="/wiki/Prudential_Financial" title="Prudential Financial">Prudential Insurance Company of America</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BowieBond3_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BowieBond3-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AP97_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP97-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> The bonds paid an interest rate of 7.9% and had an average life of ten years,<sup id="cite_ref-upennalumni_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-upennalumni-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> a higher rate of return than a 10-year <a href="/wiki/Treasury_note" class="mw-redirect" title="Treasury note">Treasury note</a> (at the time, 6.37%).<sup id="cite_ref-AP97_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP97-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Royalty_payment" title="Royalty payment">Royalties</a> from the 25 albums generated the cash flow that secured the bonds' interest payments.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> Prudential also received guarantees from Bowie's label, EMI Records, which had recently signed a $30m deal with Bowie.<sup id="cite_ref-AP97_145-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP97-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> By forfeiting ten years worth of royalties, Bowie received a payment of US$55&#160;million up front. Bowie used this income to buy songs owned by his former manager.<sup id="cite_ref-upennalumni_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-upennalumni-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> Bowie's combined catalogue of albums covered by this agreement sold more than 1&#160;million copies annually at the time of the agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-AP97_145-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP97-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> By March 2004, <a href="/wiki/Moody%27s_Investors_Service" title="Moody&#39;s Investors Service">Moody's Investors Service</a> lowered the bonds from an A3 rating (the seventh highest rating) to Baa3, one notch above <a href="/wiki/High-yield_debt" title="High-yield debt">junk status</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-score_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-score-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> The downgrade was prompted by lower-than-expected revenue "due to weakness in sales for recorded music" and that an unnamed company guaranteed the issue.<sup id="cite_ref-bowiebond_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowiebond-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Nonetheless, the bonds liquidated in 2007 as originally planned, without default, and the rights to the income from the songs reverted to Bowie.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="BowieNet">BowieNet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Bowie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: BowieNet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In September 1998, Bowie launched an <a href="/wiki/Internet_service_provider" title="Internet service provider">Internet service provider</a>, BowieNet, developed in conjunction with Robert Goodale and <a href="/wiki/Ron_Roy_(producer)" title="Ron Roy (producer)">Ron Roy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Stuart_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stuart-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hogan_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hogan-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> Subscribers to the <a href="/wiki/Dial-up_Internet_access" title="Dial-up Internet access">dial-up</a> service were offered exclusive content, as well as a BowieNet email address and Internet access.<sup id="cite_ref-Stuart_152-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stuart-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> The service was closed by 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-Stuart_152-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stuart-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1999.E2.80.932012:_Neoclassicist_Bowie"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1999–2012:_Neoclassicist_Bowie">1999–2012: Neoclassicist Bowie</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Bowie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 1999–2012: Neoclassicist Bowie">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heathen_Tour_Bowie_and_Sterling_Campbell.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Heathen_Tour_Bowie_and_Sterling_Campbell.jpg/220px-Heathen_Tour_Bowie_and_Sterling_Campbell.jpg" width="220" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Heathen_Tour_Bowie_and_Sterling_Campbell.jpg/330px-Heathen_Tour_Bowie_and_Sterling_Campbell.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Heathen_Tour_Bowie_and_Sterling_Campbell.jpg/440px-Heathen_Tour_Bowie_and_Sterling_Campbell.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1041" data-file-height="824" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heathen_Tour_Bowie_and_Sterling_Campbell.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bowie on stage with <a href="/wiki/Sterling_Campbell" title="Sterling Campbell">Sterling Campbell</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Heathen_Tour" title="Heathen Tour">Heathen Tour</a>, 2002</div></div></div>
<p>Bowie, with Reeves Gabrels, created the soundtrack for <i><a href="/wiki/Omikron:_The_Nomad_Soul" class="mw-redirect" title="Omikron: The Nomad Soul">Omikron: The Nomad Soul</a></i>, a 1999 computer game in which he and Iman also voiced characters based on their likenesses. Released the same year and containing re-recorded tracks from <i>Omikron</i>, his album <i><a href="/wiki/Hours_(David_Bowie_album)" title="Hours (David Bowie album)">Hours</a></i> featured a song with lyrics by the winner of his "Cyber Song Contest" Internet competition, Alex Grant.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> Making extensive use of live instruments, the album was Bowie's exit from heavy electronica.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> Sessions for the planned album <i><a href="/wiki/Toy_(David_Bowie_album)" title="Toy (David Bowie album)">Toy</a></i>, intended to feature new versions of some of Bowie's earliest pieces as well as three new songs, commenced in 2000, but the album was never released. Bowie and Visconti continued their collaboration, producing a new album of completely original songs instead: the result of the sessions was the 2002 album <i><a href="/wiki/Heathen_(David_Bowie_album)" title="Heathen (David Bowie album)">Heathen</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 25 June 2000, Bowie made his second appearance at the <a href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival" title="Glastonbury Festival">Glastonbury Festival</a> in England, playing 30 years after his first.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> On 27 June, Bowie performed a concert at <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting_House" title="Broadcasting House">BBC Radio Theatre</a> in London, which was released in the compilation album <i><a href="/wiki/Bowie_at_the_Beeb" title="Bowie at the Beeb">Bowie at the Beeb</a></i>, which also featured BBC recording sessions from 1968 to 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Bowie and Iman's daughter was born on 15 August.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2001, Bowie opened <a href="/wiki/The_Concert_for_New_York_City" title="The Concert for New York City">the Concert for New York City</a>, a charity event to benefit the victims of the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>, with a minimalist performance of <a href="/wiki/Simon_%26_Garfunkel" title="Simon &amp; Garfunkel">Simon &amp; Garfunkel</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/America_(Simon_%26_Garfunkel_song)" title="America (Simon &amp; Garfunkel song)">America</a>", followed by a full band performance of "Heroes".<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> 2002 saw the release of <i>Heathen</i>, and, during the second half of the year, the <a href="/wiki/Heathen_Tour" title="Heathen Tour">Heathen Tour</a>. Taking place in Europe and North America, the tour opened at London's annual <i><a href="/wiki/Meltdown_(festival)" title="Meltdown (festival)">Meltdown</a></i> festival, for which Bowie was that year appointed artistic director. Among the acts he selected for the festival were <a href="/wiki/Philip_Glass" title="Philip Glass">Philip Glass</a>, <a href="/wiki/Television_(band)" title="Television (band)">Television</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Dandy_Warhols" title="The Dandy Warhols">the Dandy Warhols</a>. As well as songs from the new album, the tour featured material from Bowie's <i><a href="/wiki/Low_(David_Bowie_album)" title="Low (David Bowie album)">Low</a></i> era.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Reality_(David_Bowie_album)" title="Reality (David Bowie album)">Reality</a></i> (2003) followed, and its accompanying world tour, the <a href="/wiki/A_Reality_Tour" title="A Reality Tour">A Reality Tour</a>, with an estimated attendance of 722,000, grossed more than any other in 2004. Onstage in <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a>, Norway, on 18 June, Bowie was hit in the eye with a lollipop thrown by a fan; a week later he suffered chest pain while performing at the <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Festival" title="Hurricane Festival">Hurricane Festival</a> in <a href="/wiki/Schee%C3%9Fel" title="Scheeßel">Scheeßel</a>, Germany. Originally thought to be a pinched nerve in his shoulder, the pain was later diagnosed as an acutely blocked <a href="/wiki/Coronary_circulation" title="Coronary circulation">coronary artery</a>, requiring an emergency <a href="/wiki/Angioplasty" title="Angioplasty">angioplasty</a> in Hamburg. The remaining 14 dates of the tour were cancelled.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> That same year, his interest in <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> led him to support the <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_Buddhism" title="Tibetan Buddhism">Tibetan</a> cause by performing at a concert to support the New York <a href="/wiki/Tibet_House" title="Tibet House">Tibet House</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Duncan_Jones_and_David_Bowie_at_the_premiere_of_Moon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Duncan_Jones_and_David_Bowie_at_the_premiere_of_Moon.jpg/220px-Duncan_Jones_and_David_Bowie_at_the_premiere_of_Moon.jpg" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Duncan_Jones_and_David_Bowie_at_the_premiere_of_Moon.jpg/330px-Duncan_Jones_and_David_Bowie_at_the_premiere_of_Moon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Duncan_Jones_and_David_Bowie_at_the_premiere_of_Moon.jpg/440px-Duncan_Jones_and_David_Bowie_at_the_premiere_of_Moon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2804" data-file-height="1932" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Duncan_Jones_and_David_Bowie_at_the_premiere_of_Moon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bowie with his son <a href="/wiki/Duncan_Jones" title="Duncan Jones">Duncan Jones</a> at the premiere of Jones's directorial debut <i><a href="/wiki/Moon_(film)" title="Moon (film)">Moon</a></i>, 2009</div></div></div>
<p>In the years following his recuperation from the heart attack, Bowie reduced his musical output, making only one-off appearances on stage and in the studio. He sang in a duet of his 1971 song "<a href="/wiki/Changes_(David_Bowie_song)" title="Changes (David Bowie song)">Changes</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Butterfly_Boucher" title="Butterfly Boucher">Butterfly Boucher</a> for the 2004 animated film <i><a href="/wiki/Shrek_2" title="Shrek 2">Shrek 2</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During a relatively quiet 2005, he recorded the vocals for the song "(She Can) Do That", co-written with <a href="/wiki/BT_(musician)" title="BT (musician)">Brian Transeau</a>, for the film <i><a href="/wiki/Stealth_(film)" title="Stealth (film)">Stealth</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> He returned to the stage on 8 September 2005, appearing with <a href="/wiki/Arcade_Fire" title="Arcade Fire">Arcade Fire</a> for the US nationally televised event Fashion Rocks, and performed with the Canadian band for the second time a week later during the <a href="/wiki/CMJ" title="CMJ">CMJ</a> Music Marathon.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> He contributed backing vocals on <a href="/wiki/TV_on_the_Radio" title="TV on the Radio">TV on the Radio</a>'s song "Province" for their album <i><a href="/wiki/Return_to_Cookie_Mountain" title="Return to Cookie Mountain">Return to Cookie Mountain</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> made a commercial with <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a> for <a href="/wiki/XM_Satellite_Radio" title="XM Satellite Radio">XM Satellite Radio</a><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> and joined with Lou Reed on Danish alt-rockers <a href="/wiki/Kashmir_(band)" title="Kashmir (band)">Kashmir's</a> 2005 album <i><a href="/wiki/No_Balance_Palace" title="No Balance Palace">No Balance Palace</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bowie was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Lifetime_Achievement_Award" title="Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award">Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award</a> on 8 February 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> In April, he announced, "I'm taking a year off—no touring, no albums."<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> He made a surprise guest appearance at <a href="/wiki/David_Gilmour" title="David Gilmour">David Gilmour</a>'s 29 May concert at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a> in London. The event was recorded, and a selection of songs on which he had contributed joint vocals were subsequently released.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> He performed again in November, alongside <a href="/wiki/Alicia_Keys" title="Alicia Keys">Alicia Keys</a>, at the Black Ball, a benefit event for <a href="/wiki/Keep_a_Child_Alive" title="Keep a Child Alive">Keep a Child Alive</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Hammerstein_Ballroom" title="Hammerstein Ballroom">Hammerstein Ballroom</a> in New York.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> The performance marked the last time Bowie performed his music on stage.<sup id="cite_ref-RS1149_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RS1149-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bowie was chosen to curate the 2007 High Line Festival, selecting musicians and artists for the <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a> event, including electronic pop duo <a href="/wiki/AIR_(French_band)" class="mw-redirect" title="AIR (French band)">AIR</a>, surrealist photographer <a href="/wiki/Claude_Cahun" title="Claude Cahun">Claude Cahun</a>, and English comedian <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Gervais" title="Ricky Gervais">Ricky Gervais</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> Bowie performed on <a href="/wiki/Scarlett_Johansson" title="Scarlett Johansson">Scarlett Johansson</a>'s 2008 album of <a href="/wiki/Tom_Waits" title="Tom Waits">Tom Waits</a> covers, <i><a href="/wiki/Anywhere_I_Lay_My_Head" title="Anywhere I Lay My Head">Anywhere I Lay My Head</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> On the 40th anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">July 1969 moon landing</a>—and Bowie's accompanying commercial breakthrough with "Space Oddity"—EMI released the individual tracks from the original eight-track studio recording of the song, in a 2009 contest inviting members of the public to create a remix.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/A_Reality_Tour_(album)" title="A Reality Tour (album)">A Reality Tour</a></i>, a double album of live material from the 2003 concert tour, was released in January 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In late March 2011, <i><a href="/wiki/Toy_(David_Bowie_album)" title="Toy (David Bowie album)">Toy</a></i>, Bowie's previously unreleased album from 2001, was leaked onto the internet, containing material used for <i>Heathen</i> and most of its single B-sides, as well as unheard new versions of his early back catalogue.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2013.E2.80.932016:_Final_years"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2013–2016:_Final_years">2013–2016: Final years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Bowie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 2013–2016: Final years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 8 January 2013, his 66th birthday, his website announced a new album, to be titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Next_Day" title="The Next Day">The Next Day</a></i> and scheduled for release 8 March for Australia, 12 March for the United States, and 11 March for the rest of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> Bowie's first studio album in a decade, <i>The Next Day</i> contains 14 songs plus 3 bonus tracks.<sup id="cite_ref-birthday_boy_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-birthday_boy-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-spin_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spin-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> His website acknowledged the length of his hiatus.<sup id="cite_ref-nmenextday_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nmenextday-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> Record producer <a href="/wiki/Tony_Visconti" title="Tony Visconti">Tony Visconti</a> said 29 tracks were recorded for the album, some of which could appear on Bowie's next record, which he might start work on later in 2013. The announcement was accompanied by the immediate release of a single, "<a href="/wiki/Where_Are_We_Now%3F" title="Where Are We Now?">Where Are We Now?</a>", written and recorded by Bowie in New York and produced by longtime collaborator Visconti.<sup id="cite_ref-nmenextday_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nmenextday-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A music video for "Where Are We Now?" was released onto <a href="/wiki/Vimeo" title="Vimeo">Vimeo</a> the same day, directed by New York artist <a href="/wiki/Tony_Oursler" title="Tony Oursler">Tony Oursler</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nmenextday_186-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nmenextday-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> The single topped the UK <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> Chart within hours of its release,<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> and debuted in the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a> at No. 6,<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> his first single to enter the Top 10 for two decades (since "<a href="/wiki/Jump_They_Say" title="Jump They Say">Jump They Say</a>" in 1993).  A second video, "The Stars (Are Out Tonight)", was released 25 February. Directed by <a href="/wiki/Floria_Sigismondi" title="Floria Sigismondi">Floria Sigismondi</a>, it stars Bowie and <a href="/wiki/Tilda_Swinton" title="Tilda Swinton">Tilda Swinton</a> as a married couple.<sup id="cite_ref-charthistory_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charthistory-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> On 1 March, the album was made available to stream for free through <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Next Day</i> debuted at No. 1 on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">UK Albums Chart</a>, was his first album to achieve that position since <i>Black Tie White Noise</i> (1993), and was the fastest-selling album of 2013 at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-nextdayukchart_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nextdayukchart-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> The music video for the song "<a href="/wiki/The_Next_Day_(song)" title="The Next Day (song)">The Next Day</a>" created some controversy, initially being removed from YouTube for <a href="/wiki/Terms_of_service" title="Terms of service">terms-of-service</a> violation, then restored with a warning recommending viewing only by those 18 or over.<sup id="cite_ref-CBS_video_controversy_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBS_video_controversy-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i>, Bowie ruled out ever giving an interview again.<sup id="cite_ref-Times_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> An exhibition of Bowie artefacts, called "<a href="/wiki/David_Bowie_Is" title="David Bowie Is">David Bowie Is</a>", was organised by the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_and_Albert_Museum" title="Victoria and Albert Museum">Victoria and Albert Museum</a> in London, and shown there in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> The London exhibit was visited by 311,956 people, making it one of the most successful exhibitions ever staged at the museum.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> Later that year the exhibition began a world tour, starting in <a href="/wiki/Art_Gallery_of_Ontario" title="Art Gallery of Ontario">Toronto</a> and including stops in <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Contemporary_Art,_Chicago" title="Museum of Contemporary Art, Chicago">Chicago</a>, Paris, Melbourne, and <a href="/wiki/Groningen" title="Groningen">Groningen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> Bowie was featured in a cameo vocal in the <a href="/wiki/Arcade_Fire" title="Arcade Fire">Arcade Fire</a> song <a href="/wiki/Reflektor_(song)" title="Reflektor (song)">"Reflektor"</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> A poll carried out by BBC History Magazine, in October 2013, named Bowie as the best-dressed Briton in history.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/2014_Brit_Awards" title="2014 Brit Awards">2014 Brit Awards</a> on 19 February, Bowie became the oldest recipient of a <a href="/wiki/Brit_Awards" title="Brit Awards">Brit Award</a> in the ceremony's history when he won the award for Best British Male, which was collected on his behalf by <a href="/wiki/Kate_Moss" title="Kate Moss">Kate Moss</a>. His speech read: "I'm completely delighted to have a Brit for being the best male – but I am, aren't I Kate? Yes. I think it's a great way to end the day. Thank you very, very much and Scotland stay with us."<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> Bowie's reference to the forthcoming September 2014 <a href="/wiki/Scottish_independence_referendum,_2014" title="Scottish independence referendum, 2014">Scottish independence referendum</a> garnered a significant reaction throughout the UK on <a href="/wiki/Social_media" title="Social media">social media</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> On 18 July, Bowie indicated that future music would be forthcoming, though he was vague about details.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>New information was released in September 2014 regarding his next compilation album, <i><a href="/wiki/Nothing_Has_Changed" title="Nothing Has Changed">Nothing Has Changed</a></i>, which was released in November. The album featured rare tracks and old material from his catalogue in addition to a new song titled "<a href="/wiki/Sue_(Or_in_a_Season_of_Crime)" title="Sue (Or in a Season of Crime)">Sue (Or in a Season of Crime)</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> In May 2015, "Let's Dance" was announced to be reissued as a yellow vinyl single on 16 July 2015 in conjunction with the "David Bowie is" exhibition at the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Centre_for_the_Moving_Image" title="Australian Centre for the Moving Image">Australian Centre for the Moving Image</a> in <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a>, Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2015, it was announced that Bowie was writing songs for a Broadway musical based on the <i><a href="/wiki/SpongeBob_SquarePants" title="SpongeBob SquarePants">SpongeBob SquarePants</a></i> cartoon series.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> Bowie wrote and recorded the opening title song to the television series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_Panthers" title="The Last Panthers">The Last Panthers</a></i>, which aired in November 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> The theme that was used for <i>The Last Panthers</i> was also the title track for his January 2016 release <i><a href="/wiki/Blackstar_(album)" title="Blackstar (album)">Blackstar</a></i> which is said to take cues from his earlier krautrock influenced work.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> According to <i>The Times</i>: "<i>Blackstar</i> may be the oddest work yet from Bowie".<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> On 7 December 2015, Bowie's musical <i><a href="/wiki/Lazarus_(musical)" title="Lazarus (musical)">Lazarus</a></i> debuted in New York. His last public appearance was at opening night of the production.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Blackstar</i> was released on 8 January 2016, Bowie's 69th birthday, and was met with critical acclaim.<sup id="cite_ref-MCblackstar_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCblackstar-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> Following his death on 10 January, producer Tony Visconti revealed that Bowie had planned the album to be his <a href="/wiki/Swan_song" title="Swan song">swan song</a>, and a "parting gift" for his fans before his death.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> Several reporters and critics subsequently noted that most of the lyrics on the album seem to revolve around his impending death,<sup id="cite_ref-CNNdeath_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNNdeath-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Billboarddeath_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboarddeath-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> noting that the album "reveals a man who appears to be grappling with his own mortality".<sup id="cite_ref-CNNdeath_214-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNNdeath-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> Visconti later said that Bowie had been planning a post-<i>Blackstar</i> album, and had written and recorded demo versions of five songs in his final weeks, suggesting that Bowie believed he had a few months left.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> The day following his death, online viewing of Bowie's music skyrocketed, breaking the record for <a href="/wiki/Vevo" title="Vevo">Vevo</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Vevo#Record_holders" title="Vevo">most viewed artist in a single day</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> On 15 January, <i>Blackstar</i> debuted at number one on the UK Albums Chart; nineteen of his albums were in the UK Top 100 Albums Chart, and thirteen singles were in the UK Top 100 Singles Chart.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> <i>Blackstar</i> also debuted at number one on album charts around the world, including Australia, France, Germany, Italy, New Zealand, and the US <i>Billboard</i> 200.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 11 January 2016, more than 1.3&#160;million people had visited the "David Bowie Is" exhibition, making it the most successful exhibition ever staged by the Victoria and Albert Museum in terms of worldwide attendance.<sup id="cite_ref-brown11jan2016_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brown11jan2016-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> The museum stated that the exhibition would continue to tour, with confirmed travel to Japan in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-brown11jan2016_222-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brown11jan2016-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/59th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="59th Annual Grammy Awards">59th Annual Grammy Awards</a>, Bowie won all five nominated awards: <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rock_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Rock Performance">Best Rock Performance</a>; <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Alternative_Music_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Alternative Music Album">Best Alternative Music Album</a>; <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Engineered_Album,_Non-Classical" title="Grammy Award for Best Engineered Album, Non-Classical">Best Engineered Album, Non-Classical</a>; <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Recording_Package" title="Grammy Award for Best Recording Package">Best Recording Package</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rock_Song" title="Grammy Award for Best Rock Song">Best Rock Song</a>. The wins marked Bowie's first ever in musical categories.<sup id="cite_ref-59thGA_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59thGA-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>An EP, <i><a href="/wiki/No_Plan_(EP)" title="No Plan (EP)">No Plan</a></i>, was released on 8 January 2017, which would have been Bowie's 70th birthday.<sup id="cite_ref-noplan_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-noplan-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> Apart from "Lazarus", the EP includes three songs that Bowie had recorded during the <i>Blackstar</i> sessions, but were left off the album and subsequently appeared on the <a href="/wiki/Lazarus_(soundtrack)" title="Lazarus (soundtrack)">soundtrack album</a> for the <i>Lazarus</i> musical in October 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-noplan2_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-noplan2-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> A music video for the title track was also released.<sup id="cite_ref-noplan2_226-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-noplan2-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> Since January 2016, Bowie has sold 5 million units in the United Kingdom alone.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Acting_career">Acting career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Bowie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Acting career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The beginnings of Bowie's acting career predate his commercial breakthrough as a musician. Studying <a href="/wiki/Avant-garde" title="Avant-garde">avant-garde</a> theatre and <a href="/wiki/Mime_artist" title="Mime artist">mime</a> under <a href="/wiki/Lindsay_Kemp" title="Lindsay Kemp">Lindsay Kemp</a>, he was given the role of Cloud in Kemp's 1967 theatrical production <i>Pierrot in Turquoise</i> (later made into the 1970 television film <i>The Looking Glass Murders</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> In the black-and-white <a href="/wiki/Short_film" title="Short film">short</a> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Image_(short_film)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Image (short film)">The Image</a></i> (1969), he played a ghostly boy who emerges from a troubled artist's painting to haunt him.<sup id="cite_ref-Buckley_2005:_p._49_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Buckley_2005:_p._49-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> The same year, the film of <a href="/wiki/Leslie_Thomas" title="Leslie Thomas">Leslie Thomas</a>'s 1966 comic novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Virgin_Soldiers" title="The Virgin Soldiers">The Virgin Soldiers</a></i> saw Bowie make a brief appearance as an extra.<sup id="cite_ref-Buckley_2005:_p._49_229-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Buckley_2005:_p._49-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> In 1976 he earned acclaim for his first major film role, portraying Thomas Jerome Newton, an alien from a dying planet, in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Man_Who_Fell_to_Earth" title="The Man Who Fell to Earth">The Man Who Fell to Earth</a></i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Roeg" title="Nicolas Roeg">Nicolas Roeg</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Just_a_Gigolo_(1978_film)" title="Just a Gigolo (1978 film)">Just a Gigolo</a></i> (1979), an Anglo-German co-production directed by <a href="/wiki/David_Hemmings" title="David Hemmings">David Hemmings</a>, saw Bowie in the lead role as Prussian officer Paul von Przygodski, who, returning from World War I, is discovered by a Baroness (<a href="/wiki/Marlene_Dietrich" title="Marlene Dietrich">Marlene Dietrich</a>) and put into her Gigolo Stable.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EMP_2015-06_Labrynth.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/EMP_2015-06_Labrynth.jpg/170px-EMP_2015-06_Labrynth.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/EMP_2015-06_Labrynth.jpg/255px-EMP_2015-06_Labrynth.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/EMP_2015-06_Labrynth.jpg/340px-EMP_2015-06_Labrynth.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2176" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EMP_2015-06_Labrynth.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bowie's costume from <i><a href="/wiki/Labyrinth_(film)" title="Labyrinth (film)">Labyrinth</a></i> at the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Pop_Culture" title="Museum of Pop Culture">Museum of Pop Culture</a>, Seattle</div></div></div>
<p>Bowie played <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Merrick" title="Joseph Merrick">Joseph Merrick</a> in the Broadway theatre production <i><a href="/wiki/The_Elephant_Man_(play)" title="The Elephant Man (play)">The Elephant Man</a></i>, which he undertook wearing no stage make-up, and which earned high praise for his expressive performance. He played the part 157 times between 1980 and 1981.<sup id="cite_ref-elephantman_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elephantman-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Christiane_F._%E2%80%93_We_Children_from_Bahnhof_Zoo" title="Christiane F. – We Children from Bahnhof Zoo">Christiane F. – We Children from Bahnhof Zoo</a></i>, a 1981 biographical film focusing on a young girl's drug addiction in <a href="/wiki/West_Berlin" title="West Berlin">West Berlin</a>, featured Bowie in a cameo appearance as himself at a concert in Germany. Its soundtrack album, <i><a href="/wiki/Christiane_F._(album)" title="Christiane F. (album)">Christiane F.</a></i> (1981), featured much material from his Berlin Trilogy albums.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> Bowie starred in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hunger_(1983_film)" title="The Hunger (1983 film)">The Hunger</a></i> (1983), with <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Deneuve" title="Catherine Deneuve">Catherine Deneuve</a> and <a href="/wiki/Susan_Sarandon" title="Susan Sarandon">Susan Sarandon</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Nagisa_Oshima" title="Nagisa Oshima">Nagisa Oshima</a>'s film the same year, <i><a href="/wiki/Merry_Christmas,_Mr._Lawrence" title="Merry Christmas, Mr. Lawrence">Merry Christmas, Mr. Lawrence</a></i>, based on <a href="/wiki/Laurens_van_der_Post" title="Laurens van der Post">Laurens van der Post</a>'s novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Seed_and_the_Sower" title="The Seed and the Sower">The Seed and the Sower</a></i>, Bowie played Major Jack Celliers, a prisoner of war in a Japanese internment camp. Bowie had a cameo in <i><a href="/wiki/Yellowbeard" title="Yellowbeard">Yellowbeard</a></i>, a 1983 pirate comedy created by <a href="/wiki/Monty_Python" title="Monty Python">Monty Python</a> members, and a small part as Colin, the <a href="/wiki/Contract_killing" title="Contract killing">hitman</a> in the 1985 film <i><a href="/wiki/Into_the_Night_(film)" title="Into the Night (film)">Into the Night</a></i>. He declined to play the villain <a href="/wiki/Max_Zorin" title="Max Zorin">Max Zorin</a> in the <a href="/wiki/James_Bond" title="James Bond">James Bond</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/A_View_to_a_Kill" title="A View to a Kill">A View to a Kill</a></i> (1985).<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Absolute_Beginners_(film)" title="Absolute Beginners (film)">Absolute Beginners</a></i> (1986), a <a href="/wiki/Rock_musical" title="Rock musical">rock musical</a> film <a href="/wiki/Film_adaptation" title="Film adaptation">adapted</a> from <a href="/wiki/Colin_MacInnes" title="Colin MacInnes">Colin MacInnes</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Absolute_Beginners_(novel)" title="Absolute Beginners (novel)">book of the same name</a> about life in late 1950s London, featured Bowie's music and presented him with a minor acting role. The same year, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Henson" title="Jim Henson">Jim Henson</a>'s dark fantasy <i><a href="/wiki/Labyrinth_(film)" title="Labyrinth (film)">Labyrinth</a></i> found him with the part of Jareth, the king of the <a href="/wiki/Goblin" title="Goblin">goblins</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> Two years later, he played <a href="/wiki/Pontius_Pilate" title="Pontius Pilate">Pontius Pilate</a> in <a href="/wiki/Martin_Scorsese" title="Martin Scorsese">Martin Scorsese</a>'s 1988 film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_Temptation_of_Christ_(film)" title="The Last Temptation of Christ (film)">The Last Temptation of Christ</a></i>. Bowie portrayed a disgruntled restaurant employee opposite <a href="/wiki/Rosanna_Arquette" title="Rosanna Arquette">Rosanna Arquette</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Linguini_Incident" title="The Linguini Incident">The Linguini Incident</a></i> (1991), and the mysterious <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">FBI</a> agent <a href="/wiki/Phillip_Jeffries" title="Phillip Jeffries">Phillip Jeffries</a> in David Lynch's <i><a href="/wiki/Twin_Peaks:_Fire_Walk_with_Me" title="Twin Peaks: Fire Walk with Me">Twin Peaks: Fire Walk with Me</a></i> (1992). He took a small but pivotal role as <a href="/wiki/Andy_Warhol" title="Andy Warhol">Andy Warhol</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Basquiat_(film)" title="Basquiat (film)">Basquiat</a></i>, artist/director <a href="/wiki/Julian_Schnabel" title="Julian Schnabel">Julian Schnabel</a>'s 1996 biopic of <a href="/wiki/Jean-Michel_Basquiat" title="Jean-Michel Basquiat">Jean-Michel Basquiat</a>, and co-starred in <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Veronesi" title="Giovanni Veronesi">Giovanni Veronesi</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Spaghetti_Western" title="Spaghetti Western">Spaghetti Western</a> <i>Il Mio West</i> (1998, released as <i><a href="/wiki/Gunslinger%27s_Revenge" title="Gunslinger&#39;s Revenge">Gunslinger's Revenge</a></i> in the US in 2005) as the most feared gunfighter in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> He played the ageing gangster Bernie in Andrew Goth's <i><a href="/wiki/Everybody_Loves_Sunshine" title="Everybody Loves Sunshine">Everybody Loves Sunshine</a></i> (1999), and appeared in the television horror series of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hunger_(TV_series)" title="The Hunger (TV series)">The Hunger</a></i>. In <i>Mr. Rice's Secret</i> (2000), he played the title role as the neighbour of a terminally ill 12-year-old, and the following year appeared as himself in <i><a href="/wiki/Zoolander" title="Zoolander">Zoolander</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bowie portrayed physicist <a href="/wiki/Nikola_Tesla" title="Nikola Tesla">Nikola Tesla</a> in <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Nolan" title="Christopher Nolan">Christopher Nolan</a>'s film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Prestige_(film)" title="The Prestige (film)">The Prestige</a></i> (2006), which was about the bitter rivalry between two magicians in the late 19th century. In the same year, he voice-acted in the animated film <i><a href="/wiki/Arthur_and_the_Invisibles" title="Arthur and the Invisibles">Arthur and the Invisibles</a></i> as the powerful villain Maltazard and appeared as himself in an episode of the <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Gervais" title="Ricky Gervais">Ricky Gervais</a> television series <i><a href="/wiki/Extras_(TV_series)" title="Extras (TV series)">Extras</a></i>. In 2007, he lent his voice to the character Lord Royal Highness in the <i><a href="/wiki/SpongeBob%27s_Atlantis_SquarePantis" title="SpongeBob&#39;s Atlantis SquarePantis">SpongeBob's Atlantis SquarePantis</a></i> television film. In the 2008 film <i><a href="/wiki/August_(2008_film)" title="August (2008 film)">August</a></i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Austin_Chick" title="Austin Chick">Austin Chick</a>, he played a supporting role as Ogilvie, alongside <a href="/wiki/Josh_Hartnett" title="Josh Hartnett">Josh Hartnett</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rip_Torn" title="Rip Torn">Rip Torn</a>, with whom he had worked in the 1976 film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Man_Who_Fell_to_Earth" title="The Man Who Fell to Earth">The Man Who Fell to Earth</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a 2017 interview with <i>Consequence of Sound</i>, director <a href="/wiki/Denis_Villeneuve" title="Denis Villeneuve">Denis Villeneuve</a> revealed his intention to cast Bowie in <i><a href="/wiki/Blade_Runner_2049" title="Blade Runner 2049">Blade Runner 2049</a></i> as the lead villain, Niander Wallace, but when news broke of Bowie's death in January of the same year, Villeneuve was forced to look for talent with similar "rock star" qualities. He eventually cast actor and lead singer of <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Seconds_to_Mars" title="Thirty Seconds to Mars">Thirty Seconds to Mars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jared_Leto" title="Jared Leto">Jared Leto</a>. Talking about the casting process, Villeneuve said: "Our first thought [for the character] had been David Bowie, who had influenced <i><a href="/wiki/Blade_Runner" title="Blade Runner">Blade Runner</a></i> in many ways. When we learned the sad news, we looked around for someone like that. He [Bowie] embodied the Blade Runner spirit."<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy_and_influence">Legacy and influence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Bowie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Legacy and influence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:David_Bowie_holywood.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/David_Bowie_holywood.jpg/220px-David_Bowie_holywood.jpg" width="220" height="192" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/David_Bowie_holywood.jpg/330px-David_Bowie_holywood.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/David_Bowie_holywood.jpg/440px-David_Bowie_holywood.jpg 2x" data-file-width="686" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:David_Bowie_holywood.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bowie's star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Berliner_Gedenktafel_Hauptstr_155_(Sch%C3%B6n)_David_Bowie.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Berliner_Gedenktafel_Hauptstr_155_%28Sch%C3%B6n%29_David_Bowie.jpg/220px-Berliner_Gedenktafel_Hauptstr_155_%28Sch%C3%B6n%29_David_Bowie.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Berliner_Gedenktafel_Hauptstr_155_%28Sch%C3%B6n%29_David_Bowie.jpg/330px-Berliner_Gedenktafel_Hauptstr_155_%28Sch%C3%B6n%29_David_Bowie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Berliner_Gedenktafel_Hauptstr_155_%28Sch%C3%B6n%29_David_Bowie.jpg/440px-Berliner_Gedenktafel_Hauptstr_155_%28Sch%C3%B6n%29_David_Bowie.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3484" data-file-height="2612" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Berliner_Gedenktafel_Hauptstr_155_(Sch%C3%B6n)_David_Bowie.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berliner_Gedenktafel" class="extiw" title="de:Berliner Gedenktafel">Berlin Memorial Plaque</a>, Hauptstraße 155, in <a href="/wiki/Sch%C3%B6neberg" title="Schöneberg">Schöneberg</a>, Germany</div></div></div>
<p>Bowie's songs and stagecraft brought a new dimension to popular music in the early 1970s, strongly influencing both its immediate forms and its subsequent development.
